National boundaries were not explicitly prescribed by the 1947 Constitution, and the Constitutional Court declined to define these boundaries in a 1993 interpretation, viewing the question as a political question to be resolved by the Executive and Legislative Yuans.[^326] The 1947 Constitution included articles regarding representatives from former Qing dynasty territories including [Tibet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tibet "Tibet") and [Mongol banners](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Banners_of_Inner_Mongolia "Banners of Inner Mongolia").[^327] [^328] [^329] The ROC recognized [Mongolia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mongolia "Mongolia") as an independent country in 1946 after signing the 1945 [Sino-Soviet Treaty of Friendship and Alliance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sino-Soviet_Treaty_of_Friendship_and_Alliance "Sino-Soviet Treaty of Friendship and Alliance"), but after retreating to Taiwan in 1949 it reneged to preserve its claim over mainland China.[^330] The Additional Articles of the 1990s did not alter national boundaries, but suspended articles regarding Mongolian and Tibetan representatives. The ROC began to accept the Mongolian passport and removed clauses referring to Outer Mongolia from the Act Governing Relations between the People of the Taiwan Area and the Mainland Area in February 2002.[^331] In October 2002, the ROC recognized Mongolia as independent and began excluding it from its official maps.[^34] In 2012 the Mainland Affairs Council issued a statement clarifying that Outer Mongolia was not part of the ROC's national territory in 1947.[^332] The [Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mongolian_and_Tibetan_Affairs_Commission "Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission") in the Executive Yuan was abolished in 2017.

### Administrative divisions

According to the 1947 constitution, the territory of the ROC is according to its "existing national boundaries".[^333] The ROC is, *de jure* constitutionally, divided into [provinces](#History), [special municipalities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special_municipality_\(Taiwan\) "Special municipality (Taiwan)") (which are further divided into districts for local administration), and the province-level [Tibet Area](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tibet_Area_\(administrative_division\) "Tibet Area (administrative division)"). Each province is subdivided into [cities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Provincial_city_\(Taiwan\) "Provincial city (Taiwan)") and [counties](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/County_\(Taiwan\) "County (Taiwan)"), which are further divided into townships and county-administered cities. Some divisions are indigenous divisions which have different degrees of autonomy to standard ones. In addition, districts, cities and townships are further divided into villages and neighborhoods.

Since its retreat, the ROC has controlled only [Taiwan Province](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taiwan_\(Republic_of_China_province\) "Taiwan (Republic of China province)") and some islands of [Fujian Province](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fujian_Province,_Republic_of_China "Fujian Province, Republic of China"), with the provincial governments now "streamlined" and no longer functional.[^334] [^335] The ROC also controls the [Pratas Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pratas_Islands "Pratas Islands") and [Taiping Island](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taiping_Island "Taiping Island") in the [Spratly Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spratly_Islands "Spratly Islands"), which are part of the disputed [South China Sea Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_China_Sea_Islands "South China Sea Islands"), and has placed them under the administration of [Kaohsiung](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kaohsiung "Kaohsiung").[^336] With provinces non-functional, Taiwan is in practice divided into 22 subnational divisions, each with a self-governing body led by an elected leader and a legislative body with elected members. Duties of local governments include social services, education, urban planning, public construction, water management, environmental protection, transport, public safety, and more.

Notes

[^1]: Has an elected executive and an elected legislative council.

[^2]: Has an appointed district administrator for managing local affairs and carrying out tasks commissioned by superior agency.

[^3]: Has an elected village administrator for managing local affairs and carrying out tasks commissioned by superior agency.

[^4]: [See here](#Words_in_native_languages) for other local languages

[^5]: In October 2002, the ROC recognized Mongolia as independent and began excluding it from its official maps.[^34]

[^6]: [Taipei](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taipei "Taipei") is the official seat of [government of the Republic of China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Government_of_the_Republic_of_China "Government of the Republic of China") although the [Constitution of the Republic of China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Republic_of_China "Constitution of the Republic of China") does not specify the *de jure* capital.[^35]

[^7]: [Mandarin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taiwanese_Mandarin "Taiwanese Mandarin") as the standard [variety of Chinese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Variety_of_Chinese "Variety of Chinese") [^37]  
[Vernacular Chinese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vernacular_Chinese "Vernacular Chinese") (used in most occasions)  
[Classical Chinese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Classical_Chinese "Classical Chinese") (used in formal or ceremonial occasions, religious or cultural rites, official documents, legal and court rulings and judiciary documents) [^38]

[^8]: A national language in Taiwan is legally defined as "a natural language used by an original people group of Taiwan and the [Taiwan Sign Language](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taiwan_Sign_Language "Taiwan Sign Language") ".[^43]

[^9]: Not designated but meets legal definition.

[^10]: Colloquially known as "Taiwanese", it is considered a variety of [Hokkien](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hokkien "Hokkien").

[^11]: Mixed indigenous-Han ancestry is included in the figure for Han.

[^12]: While the [tricameral parliament](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tricameralism "Tricameralism") continues to exist *de jure*, the [National Assembly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Assembly_\(Republic_of_China\) "National Assembly (Republic of China)") (electoral college) was *de facto* suspended in 2005 and the [Control Yuan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Control_Yuan "Control Yuan") (upper house) ceased to be a parliamentary chamber *de facto* in 1993 leaving the Legislative Yuan (lower house) as the *de facto* unicameral chamber.

[^13]: The [HDI annual report](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_Development_Report "Human Development Report") compiled by the [UNDP](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UNDP "UNDP") does not include Taiwan because it is no longer a UN member state, and is neither included as part of the People's Republic of China by both of the UNDP and SHDI reports when calculating data for China.[^56] [Taiwan's Statistical Bureau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Directorate_General_of_Budget,_Accounting_and_Statistics "Directorate General of Budget, Accounting and Statistics") calculated its HDI for 2023 to be 0.934 based on UNDP's 2014 methodology, which would place Taiwan at 21st globally in 2023 within the 2025 UNDP report.[^57]

[^14]: There are four contemporary geopolitical definitions of the extent of "Taiwan":

1. The common name referring to the state, also known as the "Republic of China" (ROC), including [all 168 islands administered by the ROC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_islands_of_Taiwan "List of islands of Taiwan"), collectively known as [Taiwan Area](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taiwan_Area "Taiwan Area");[^59]
2. The traditional Taiwan region (本島地區), which consists of the main island of Taiwan and its surrounding islands, including the [Penghu islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Penghu_islands "Penghu islands"),[^60] [^61] but excludes [Kinmen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kinmen "Kinmen"), [Matsu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matsu_Islands "Matsu Islands"), and [Wuqiu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wuqiu,_Kinmen "Wuqiu, Kinmen"), those are traditionally parts of [Fujian Province](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fuchien_Province,_Republic_of_China "Fuchien Province, Republic of China"), and also excluding the ROC-controlled [South China Sea Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_China_Sea_Islands "South China Sea Islands");
3. The traditional region without Penghu, which is sometimes regarded as a separate region;
4. The main island of Taiwan (Formosa) alone, excluding all the offshore islands nearby.

[^15]: Bellwood's definition: "Island Southeast Asia includes Taiwan, the Philippines, Brunei and the Sarawak and Sabah provinces of East Malaysia (northern Borneo), and all of the islands of Indonesia to the west of New Guinea."

[^16]: Robert Blust: "The major western island groups include the great Indonesian, or Malay Archipelago, to its north the smaller and more compact Philippine Archipelago, and still further north at 22 to 25 degrees north latitude and some 150 kilometres from the coast of China, the island of Taiwan (Formosa). Together these island groups constitute insular (or island) Southeast Asia."

[^17]: Despite the conventional definition to include Taiwan as part of East Asia, there is some variability as to whether Taiwan is also included in the region of [Maritime Southeast Asia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maritime_Southeast_Asia "Maritime Southeast Asia"). Some scholars, such as [Peter Bellwood](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_Bellwood "Peter Bellwood") and [Robert Blust](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Blust "Robert Blust"),[^63] [^15] [^16] include Taiwan as part of [Southeast Asia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southeast_Asia "Southeast Asia") in their definition.

[^18]: According to official data from [Executive Yuan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Executive_Yuan "Executive Yuan") and local governments of Taiwan, [Taiwan Area](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taiwan_Area "Taiwan Area") consists of total 168 naturally occurring islands.

1. Taiwan (Formosa) and its offshore islands (22) [^64]
2. [Penghu Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Penghu_Islands "Penghu Islands") (90) [^65] [^66]
3. [Kinmen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kinmen "Kinmen"), including [Wuqiu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wuqiu,_Kinmen "Wuqiu, Kinmen") (17) [^67] [^68] [^69]
4. [Matsu Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matsu_Islands "Matsu Islands") (36) [^70] [^71]
5. [Pratas Island](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pratas_Island "Pratas Island") (1) [^72] [^73]
6. [Spratly Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spratly_Islands "Spratly Islands") (2, [Taiping](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taiping_Island "Taiping Island") and [Zhongzhou](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zhongzhou_Reef "Zhongzhou Reef"))

Note: The [Senkaku Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Senkaku_Islands "Senkaku Islands") (known as "Diaoyu" or "Diaoyutai" in standard Chinese), which are an archipelago of 8 islands and islets in the East China Sea, are controlled by Japan, and are [disputed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Senkaku_Islands_dispute "Senkaku Islands dispute") by the ROC and the PRC (People's Republic of China) as being a part of Taiwan. Japan administers the Senkaku Islands as a part of the [Ryukyu Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ryukyu_Islands "Ryukyu Islands").

[^19]: The [HDI annual report](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_Development_Report "Human Development Report") compiled by the [UNDP](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UNDP "UNDP") does not include Taiwan because it is no longer a UN member state, and is neither included as part of the People's Republic of China by the UNDP when calculating data for China.[^80] [Taiwan's Statistical Bureau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Directorate_General_of_Budget,_Accounting_and_Statistics "Directorate General of Budget, Accounting and Statistics") calculated its HDI for 2021 to be 0.926 based on UNDP's 2010 methodology,[^81] [^82] which would place Taiwan at 19th globally in 2021 within the 2022 UNDP report.[^83] [^84]

[^20]: Although this is the present meaning of *guó*, in [Old Chinese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Chinese "Old Chinese") (when its pronunciation was something like /\*qʷˤək/) [^102] it meant the walled city of the Chinese and the areas they could control from them.[^103]

[^21]: Its use is attested from the sixth-century [Classic of History](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Classic_of_History "Classic of History"), which states " [Huangtian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tian_\(god\) "Tian (god)") bestowed the lands and the peoples of the central state to the ancestors" (皇天既付中國民越厥疆土于先王).[^104]

[^22]: Interpretations on whether sovereignty was transferred to the ROC varies. ROC took control of Taiwan under [General Order No. 1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_Order_No._1 "General Order No. 1"), on behalf of the [Allies of World War II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II "Allies of World War II"). Taiwan was simultaneously established as a [ROC province](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taiwan_\(Republic_of_China_province\) "Taiwan (Republic of China province)"), though opinions differed among the Allies on the unilateral announcement of annexation of Taiwan by the ROC. Japan later renounced its claims to Taiwan and the Pescadores in the [Treaty of San Francisco](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_San_Francisco "Treaty of San Francisco") in 1952; see [Retrocession Day](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Retrocession_Day "Retrocession Day"), [Theory of the Undetermined Status of Taiwan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theory_of_the_Undetermined_Status_of_Taiwan "Theory of the Undetermined Status of Taiwan"), [political status of Taiwan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_status_of_Taiwan "Political status of Taiwan") and [1943 Cairo Declaration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1943_Cairo_Declaration "1943 Cairo Declaration").

[^23]: Also known as the Taiwan area or Tai–Min area ([Chinese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_characters "Traditional Chinese characters"): 臺閩地區; lit. 'Taiwan–Fujian area')

[^24]: The mainland area consists of Mainland China, [Tibet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tibet "Tibet") and (previously) [Outer Mongolia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Outer_Mongolia "Outer Mongolia")

[^25]: Special municipalities, cities, and county-administered cities are all called *shi* ([Chinese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_characters "Traditional Chinese characters"): 市; lit. 'city')

[^26]: Nominal; provincial governments have been abolished

[^27]: Constitutionally having the same structure as the free area, these are currently under the [Chinese Communist Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chinese_Communist_Party "Chinese Communist Party") control with a different structure

[^28]: Sometimes called cities ([Chinese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_characters "Traditional Chinese characters"): 市) or provincial cities ([Chinese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_characters "Traditional Chinese characters"): 省轄市) to distinguish them from special municipalities and county-administered cities

[^29]: There are two types of townships: rural townships or *xīang* ([Chinese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_characters "Traditional Chinese characters"): 鄉) and urban townships or *zhèn* ([Chinese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_characters "Traditional Chinese characters"): 鎮)

[^30]: Villages in rural townships are known as *cūn* ([Chinese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_characters "Traditional Chinese characters"): 村), those in other jurisdictions are known as *lǐ* ([Chinese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_characters "Traditional Chinese characters"): 里)

[^31]: In local languages:

- [Traditional Chinese script](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_characters "Traditional Chinese characters"): 臺灣, 台灣
- [Mandarin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taiwanese_Mandarin "Taiwanese Mandarin") [Pinyin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pinyin "Pinyin"): *Táiwān*
- [Hokkien](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taiwanese_Hokkien "Taiwanese Hokkien"): *Tâi-uân*
- [Sixian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sixian_dialect "Sixian dialect") Hakka: *Tǒi-vǎn*
- [Amis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amis_language "Amis language"): *Taywan*
- [Paiwan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paiwan_language "Paiwan language"): *Taiwan*

[^32]: In local languages:

- [Traditional Chinese script](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_characters "Traditional Chinese characters"): 中華民國
- [Mandarin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taiwanese_Mandarin "Taiwanese Mandarin") [Pinyin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pinyin "Pinyin"): *Zhōnghuá Mínguó*
- [Hokkien](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taiwanese_Hokkien "Taiwanese Hokkien"): *Tiong-hûa Bîn-kok*
- [Sixian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sixian_dialect "Sixian dialect") Hakka: *Chûng-fà Mìn-koet*

[^33]: In local languages:

- [Traditional Chinese script](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_characters "Traditional Chinese characters"): 驅除韃虜, 恢復中華, 創立民國, 平均地權
- [Mandarin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taiwanese_Mandarin "Taiwanese Mandarin") [Pinyin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pinyin "Pinyin"): *Qūchú dálǔ, huīfù Zhōnghuá, chuànglì mínguó, píngjūn dì quán*

[^34]: ["Mongolian office to ride into Taipei by end of the year"](https://www.taipeitimes.com/News/taiwan/archives/2002/10/11/0000175237). *[Taipei Times](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taipei_Times "Taipei Times")*. 11 October 2002. [Archived](https://web.archive.org/web/20251230142705/https://www.taipeitimes.com/News/taiwan/archives/2002/10/11/0000175237) from the original on 30 December 2025. Retrieved 29 December 2025. After the Ministry of the Interior's recent decision to exclude Mongolia from the official ROC map, on Oct. 3, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs announced that Taiwan recognizes Mongolia as an independent country – 81 years after Mongolia declared its independence.

Thus, Taiwan is in fact a sovereign country from our perspective.

[^97]: [Mair, Victor H.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Victor_H._Mair "Victor H. Mair") (2003). ["How to Forget Your Mother Tongue and Remember Your National Language"](http://pinyin.info/readings/mair/taiwanese.html). *Pīnyīn.info*. [Archived](https://web.archive.org/web/20141213183153/http://pinyin.info/readings/mair/taiwanese.html) from the original on 13 December 2014. Retrieved 5 April 2018. The true derivation of the name "Taiwan" is actually from the ethnonym of a tribe in the southwest part of the island in the area around Ping'an. As early as 1636, a Dutch missionary referred to this group as Taiouwang. From the name of the tribe, the Portuguese called the area around Ping'an as Tayowan, Taiyowan, Tyovon, Teijoan, Toyouan, and so forth. Indeed, already in his ship's log of 1622, the Dutchman Cornelis Reijersen referred to the area as Teijoan and Taiyowan.

In Taiwan, the only known Paleolithic burial recovered so far comes from the Xiaoma cave complex in the southeast of the island, this being an adult male buried in a crouched posture about 4000 bce. My research with Matsumura suggests that this individual was of Australo‐Papuan affinity, most closely related with Negrito populations in the Philippines. pp. 234–235.

[^119]: Matsukusa, Hirotaka; Oota, Hiroki; Haneji, Kuniaki; et al. (2010). "A Genetic Analysis of the Sakishima Islanders Reveals No Relationship With Taiwan Aborigines but Shared Ancestry With Ainu and Main-Island Japanese". *American Journal of Physical Anthropology*. **142** (2): 211–223. [Bibcode](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bibcode_\(identifier\) "Bibcode (identifier)"):[2010AJPA..142..211M](https://ui.adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2010AJPA..142..211M). [doi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doi_\(identifier\) "Doi (identifier)"):[10.1002/ajpa.21212](https://doi.org/10.1002%2Fajpa.21212). [PMID](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PMID_\(identifier\) "PMID (identifier)") [20091849](https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/20091849). This study reveals that the Sakishima islanders are not related to Taiwan aborigines, but exhibit affinity with the Hokkaido Ainu. These results confirm that the Austronesian expansion did not contribute to modern Sakishima, main-island Okinawa, and Honshu Japanese people.

[^120]: Sato, Takehiro; Nakagome, Shigeki; Watanabe, Chiaki; Yamaguchi, Kyoko (2014). "Genome-Wide SNP Analysis Reveals Population Structure and Demographic History of the Ryukyu Islanders in the Southern Part of the Japanese Archipelago". *Molecular Biology and Evolution*. **31** (11): 2929–2940. [doi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doi_\(identifier\) "Doi (identifier)"):[10.1093/molbev/msu230](https://doi.org/10.1093%2Fmolbev%2Fmsu230). [PMID](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PMID_\(identifier\) "PMID (identifier)") [25086001](https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/25086001). A previous study based on mtDNA, Y chromosomal STRs, and autosomal STRs also showed that there was no evidence of any contribution from the aboriginal Taiwanese populations to the gene pool of the Ryukyu Islanders. Similarly, using a large number of SNP markers, this study verified that there is a clear genetic gap between Taiwan and the Ryukyu Islands.

It is their purpose that Japan shall be stripped of all the islands in the Pacific which she has seized or occupied since the beginning of the first World War in 1914, and that all the territories Japan has stolen from the Chinese, such as Manchuria, Formosa, and The Pescadores, shall be restored to the Republic of China.

The party first applied Sun's concept of political tutelage by governing through martial law, not tolerating opposition parties, controlling the public media, and using the 1947 constitution drawn up on the China mainland to govern. Although this party \[the KMT\] had initiated a democratic breakthrough and guided the democratic transition, it had also upheld martial law for thirty-six years and severely repressed political dissent and any efforts to establish an opposition party.... How was it possible that this party, so hated by opposition politicians and long regarded by Western critics as a dictatorial, Leninist-type party, still remained in power?

[^484]: Lo, Yun-Hua (2021). ["Detecting Genetic Ancestry and Adaptation in the Taiwanese Han People"](https://academic.oup.com/mbe/article/38/10/4149/5955855). *[Molecular Biology and Evolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molecular_Biology_and_Evolution "Molecular Biology and Evolution")*. **38** (10): 4149–4165. [doi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doi_\(identifier\) "Doi (identifier)"):[10.1093/molbev/msaa276](https://doi.org/10.1093%2Fmolbev%2Fmsaa276). [PMC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PMC_\(identifier\) "PMC (identifier)") [8476137](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC8476137). [PMID](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PMID_\(identifier\) "PMID (identifier)") [33170928](https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/33170928). Retrieved 18 October 2022. Consequently, our results showed that the ISEA ancestry in the Taiwanese Han was the outcome of population mixtures rather than shared ancestry, and the admixture event likely occurred before the Taiwanese Han ancestors migrated to Taiwan (fig. 2A). If the admixture occurred only after the Han people migrated to Taiwan, then the observed results would only be seen in the Taiwanese Han. However, similar F3 outcomes were found in the Chinese Han (supplementary fig. S2, Supplementary Material online), supporting that admixture occurred prior to migration to Taiwan. Moreover, signatures of population admixture were also detected between the ancestors of Taiwanese Han and the Ami Austronesian-speaking population using the F4 test; significant positive F4 values were observed when most Sino-Tibetan speaking populations were individually included in the analysis, except for the Chinese Singapore and Chinese Cantonese (table 1). These two populations appear to be genetically closest to the Taiwanese Han among all other Sino-Tibetan speaking populations (fig. 1B), which is consistent with the hypothesis of population mixture before the ancestors of Taiwanese Han migrated to Taiwan.
